             1: import math
 2: groupA = [[4, 6] ,[5,7] ,[5,8] ,[5.8,6] ,[6,6] ,[6,7] ,[7,5] ,[7,7] ,[8,4] ,[9,5]]
 3: groupB = [[2,2] ,[4,2] ,[4,4] ,[5,4] ,[5,3] ,[6,2]]
 4: a = int(input())
 5: b = int(input())
 6: sumx = 0
 7: sumy = 0
 8: for i in groupA:
 9:   for j in i:
10:     if j == i[0]:
11:       sumx += j
12:     else:
13:       sumy += j
14: x = sumx/10
15: y = sumy/10
16: ans1 = math.sqrt((a-x)*(a-x)+(b-y)*(b-y))
17: sumx = 0
18: sumy = 0
19: for i in groupB:
20:   for j in i:
21:     if j == i[0]:
22:       sumx += j
23:     else:
24:       sumy += j
25: x = sumx/10
26: y = sumy/10
27: ans2 = math.sqrt((a-x)*(a-x)+(b-y)*(b-y))
28: if ans1 < ans2:
29:   print('A')
30: else:
31:   print('B')

           1: import math
 2: groupA = [[4, 6] ,[5,7] ,[5,8] ,[5.8,6] ,[6,6] ,[6,7] ,[7,5] ,[7,7] ,[8,4] ,[9,5]]
 3: groupB = [[2,2] ,[4,2] ,[4,4] ,[5,4] ,[5,3] ,[6,2]]
 4: a = int(input())
 5: b = int(input())
 6: sumx = 0
 7: sumy = 0
 8: for i in groupA:
 9:   for j in i:
10:     if j == i[0]:
11:       sumx += j
12:     else:
13:       sumy += j
14: x = sumx/10
15: y = sumy/10
16: ans1 = math.sqrt((a-x)*(a-x)+(b-y)*(b-y))
17: sumx = 0
18: sumy = 0
19: for i in groupB:
20:   for j in i:
21:     if j == i[0]:
22:       sumx += j
23:     else:
24:       sumy += j
25: x = sumx/10
26: y = sumy/10
27: ans2 = math.sqrt((a-x)*(a-x)+(b-y)*(b-y))
28: if ans1 < ans2:
29:   print('A')
30: else:
31:   print('B')

      ä½¿ç”¨colabçš„è©±ï¼Œæ•™è‚²å¸³è™Ÿä¸ä¸€å®šå¥½ç”¨ï¼Œé€™æ¶‰åŠGoogleæä¾›çš„å…è²»è¨ˆç®—é‡(å¯èƒ½ä»¥å­¸æ ¡å–®ä½è¨ˆ)

      1. äººè‡‰åµæ¸¬å¯¦ä½œ(ç…§ç‰‡)
         1: import dlib
 2: import cv2
 3: import imutils
 4: import matplotlib.pyplot as plt
 5: # 如果是在 Google Colab上執行..
 6: # from google.colab.patches import v2_imshow
 7: # 讀照片檔
 8: img = cv2.imread('/Users/letranger/Downloads/girls.jpg')
 9: # 縮小圖片
10: img = imutils.resize(img, width=800)
11: # 人臉偵測(偵測正面)
12: detector = dlib.get_frontal_face_detector()
13: face_rects = detector(img, 1)
14: img = cv2.cvtColor(img, cv2.COLOR_BGR2RGB) #改變色調/OpenCV的顏色對照順序為BGR
15: #img = cv2.cvtColor(img, cv2.COLOR_BGR2GRAY) #灰階
16: print(face_rects)
17: # 取出所有的偵測結果
18: # Fonts
19: from PIL import ImageFont, ImageDraw, Image
20: import numpy as np
21: fontpath = 'images/NotoSansTC-Medium.otf'
22: font = ImageFont.truetype(fontpath, 18)
23: for i, d in enumerate(face_rects):
24:     x1, y1 = d.left(), d.top()
25:     x2, y2 = d.right(), d.bottom()
26:     cv2.rectangle(img, (x1, y1), (x2, y2), (0, 255, 0), 4, cv2.LINE_AA)
27:     # 以方框標示偵測的人臉、儲存
28: 
29:     #image = cv2.imread('Users/letranger/Downloads/outout.jpg)')
30:     #cv2_imshow(image)
31:     #cv2.putText(img, 'id'+str(i), (x1-10, y1-10), cv2.FONT_HERSHEY_SIMPLEX, 0.7, (0, 0, 255), 2)
32: #處理中文: pillow
33: imgPil = Image.fromarray(img)
34: draw = ImageDraw.Draw(imgPil)
35: for i, d in enumerate(face_rects):
36:     x1, y1 = d.left(), d.top()
37:     x2, y2 = d.right(), d.bottom()
38:     draw.text((x1, y1-25), '編號:'+str(i), fill=(255,255,255), font=font)
39: #img = np.array(imgPil)
40: #cv2.imwrite('/Users/letranger/Downloads/output1.jpg', img)

      2. äººè‡‰åµæ¸¬å¯¦ä½œ(webcam)
         1: import cv2
 2: import numpy as np
 3: import dlib
 4: 
 5: 
 6: # Connects to your computer's default camera
 7: cap = cv2.VideoCapture(0)
 8: # Detect the coordinates
 9: detector = dlib.get_frontal_face_detector()
10: 
11: 
12: # Capture frames continuously
13: while True:
14: 
15:     # Capture frame-by-frame
16:     ret, frame = cap.read()
17:     frame = cv2.flip(frame, 1)
18: 
19:     # RGB to grayscale
20:     gray = cv2.cvtColor(frame, cv2.COLOR_BGR2GRAY)
21:     faces = detector(gray)
22: 
23:     # Iterator to count faces
24:     i = 0
25:     for face in faces:
26: 
27:         # Get the coordinates of faces
28:         x, y = face.left(), face.top()
29:         x1, y1 = face.right(), face.bottom()
30:         cv2.rectangle(frame, (x, y), (x1, y1), (0, 255, 0), 2)
31: 
32:         # Increment iterator for each face in faces
33:         i = i+1
34: 
35:         # Display the box and faces
36:         cv2.putText(frame, 'face num'+str(i), (x-10, y-10),
37:         cv2.FONT_HERSHEY_SIMPLEX, 0.7, (0, 0, 255), 2)
38:         print(face, i)
39: 
40:     # Display the resulting frame
41:     cv2.imshow('frame', frame)
42: 
43:     # This command let's us quit with the "q" button on a keyboard.
44:     if cv2.waitKey(1) & 0xFF == ord('q'):
45:         break
46: 
47: 
48: # Release the capture and destroy the windows
49: cap.release()
50: cv2.destroyAllWindows()

      Figure 130: Caption

      èƒŒé¢åŸç†ç‚ºç‰©å“è¼ªå»“èˆ‡é¢ç©çš„æ¦‚å¿µï¼Œå¯ä»¥æ‡‰ç”¨åœ¨æ ¡åœ’é›»å­åœç±¬ã€æ€•å­¸ç”Ÿè·‘å‡ºå»ã€æ€•å£äººè·‘é€²ä¾†

      1. å¯¦ä½œ

        ipynbç‰ˆ

         1: import dlib
 2: # 如果是在 Google Colab上執行..
 3: # !pip install opencv-python==4.5.1.45 -i https://pypi.douban.com/simple
 4: # from google.colab.patches import v2_imshow
 5: from IPython.display import clear_output
 6: import cv2
 7: import numpy as np
 8: 
 9: # 讀照片檔
10: cap = cv2.VideoCapture('/Users/letranger/Downloads/nest.mp4')
11: # 縮小圖片
12: width = 600
13: height = 450
14: fourcc = cv2.VideoWriter_fourcc('m', 'p', '4', 'v')
15: out = cv2.VideoWriter('/Users/letranger/Downloads/output.mp4', fourcc, 30, (width, height))  # 30:每秒幀數
16: # 設定擷取影像的尺寸大小
17: cap.set(cv2.CAP_PROP_FRAME_WIDTH, width)
18: cap.set(cv2.CAP_PROP_FRAME_HEIGHT, height)
19: area = width * height
20: 
21: # 初始化平均影像
22: ret, frame = cap.read()
23: avg = cv2.blur(frame, (4, 4))
24: avg_float = np.float32(avg)
25: i = 0
26: while (cap.isOpened()):
27:     # 讀取一幅影格
28:     rec, frame = cap.read()
29:     # 若讀至影片結尾則跳出while
30:     if rec == False:
31:         break
32:     # 模糊處理
33:     blur = cv2.blur(frame, (4, 4))
34:     # 計算目前影格與平均影像的差異值
35:     diff = cv2.absdiff(avg, blur)
36:     # 將圖片轉為灰階(易於做邊界處理)
37:     gray = cv2.cvtColor(diff, cv2.COLOR_BGR2GRAY)
38:     # 篩選出變動程度大於門檻值的區域
39:     ret, thresh = cv2.threshold(gray, 25, 25, cv2.THRESH_BINARY)
40:     # 使用型態轉換函數去除雜訊
41:     kernel = np.ones((5, 5), np.uint8)
42:     thresh = cv2.morphologyEx(thresh, cv2.MORPH_OPEN, kernel, iterations=2)
43:     thresh = cv2.morphologyEx(thresh, cv2.MORPH_CLOSE, kernel, iterations=2)
44:     # 產生等高線
45:     cnts, cntImg = cv2.findContours(thresh.copy(), cv2.RETR_EXTERNAL, cv2.CHAIN_APPROX_SIMPLE)
46:     for c in cnts:
47:         # 忽略太小的區域(圖像差異不大)
48:         if cv2.contourArea(c) < 9000:
49:             continue
50:         # 計算等高線的外框範圍
51:         (x, y, w, h) = cv2.boundingRect(c)
52:         # 畫出外框
53:         cv2.rectangle(frame, (x, y), (x + w, y + h), (0, 255, 0), 2)
54:         if cv2.contourArea(c) > 120000:
55:             cv2.putText(frame, 'WARNING', (10, 200), cv2.FONT_HERSHEY_TRIPLEX, 1, (0, 0, 255), 1, cv.LINE)
56:         # 畫等高線
57:         cv2.drawContours(frame, cnts, -1, (0, 255, 255), 4)
58:         # save
59:         frame = cv2.resize(frame, (width, height))
60:         out.write(frame)
61:         # 顯示偵測結果影像
62:         cv2.imshow("TEST", frame)
63:         clear_output(wait=True)
64: 
65:         if cv2.waitKey(1) & 0xFF == ord('q'):
66:             break
67:         # 更新平均影像
68:         cv2.accumulateWeighted(blur, avg_float, 0.01)
69:         avg = cv2.convertScaleAbs(avg_float)
70: cap.release()
71: out.release()
72: '''
73: from IPython.display import HTML
74: from base64 import b64encode
75: import os
76: save_path = "/Users/letranger/Downloads/nest.mp4"
77: compressed_path = "/Users/letranger/Downloads/output.mp4"
78: os.system(f"ffmpeg -i {save_path} -vcodec libx264 {compressed_path}")
79: mp4=open(compressed_path, 'rb').read()
80: data_url = "data:video/mp4;base64," + b64encode(mp4).decode()
81: HTML("""
82: <video width=480 controls>
83:     <source src="%s" type="video/mp4">
84: </video>
85: """ % data_url)
86: 
87: '''

        åŠŸèƒ½åƒæ•¸è§£èªª

        • cv2.threshold(img, é–¥å€¼, æœ€å¤§ç°åº¦å€¼, ä½¿ç”¨çš„äºŒå€¼åŒ–æ–¹æ³•)
        • cnts, cntImg = cv2.findContours(thresh.copy(), cv2.RETR_EXTERNAL, cv2.CHAIN_APPROX_SIMPLE)
          • findContourç²å–è¼ªå»“ï¼Œæœƒå›å‚³å…©å€‹å€¼ï¼šç¬¬ä¸€å€‹åƒæ•¸è¼ªå»“ç·š (cnts)å’Œåœ–ç‰‡(å°è§’ç·šå–æ¡†)

    Top 6 reasons you should learn to code in 2021:

    1. Attractive salaries

    The good news for computer programmers is that most jobs youâ€™ll be interested in with your new skills pay well. In fact, the median salary of a computer programmer in the U.S. stands at $86,550 per year. Of course, salaries may vary for entry-level positions.Â 

    Because technology doesnâ€™t appear to be slowing down any time soon, learning to program also has the ability to increase your earning potential. Over time, you could get a raise, explore other career opportunities, or start your own side hustle, for instance.

    Jumpstart your way to the skills you need for a new career by starting a coding bootcamp.

    1. Have valuable skills on your resume

    Computer programming is a desirable skill because so much of our world is automated online. As a computer programmer, you will write and test code to create websites and software programs or to keep programs running and functioning well. Your goal is to innovate and continuously improve upon existing processes.

    Coding skills can improve how you do business. This is valuable to potential employers. For instance, an e-commerce business owner not only needs a website, but they need someone to collect data about how users interact with a page and modify page elements accordingly, leading to increased sales down the road.

    Even if youâ€™re in a non-coding role, knowing how to write code can be of use. For instance, you may have a degree in biology and work with a research lab. Knowing how to code could allow you to participate in application and software development for your company as well as other private and government agencies. Likewise, a psychologist who knows how to code may be able to create a mobile app to help people monitor their depression and anxiety symptoms.

    Common skills of effective computer programmers:

    Proficiency in at least one programming language

    Problem-solving, logic, and critical thinking skills

    Attention to detail and focus

    Effective communicators

    Lifelong learners excited by new technology

    1. Choose from many job offers

    There are plenty of programming jobs for you to pursue in the world of technology. Perhaps youâ€™d like to spend entire days writing code from home. You can do that! You can also use your programming knowledge to drive business decisions.

    Some popular jobs that require coding are software application developers, web developers, and computer systems engineers. See careers for computer programmers to explore more options.

    Even in fields where coding isnâ€™t required, achieving fluency in coding can help increase your marketability. Read these tips from recruiters to find out how you can stand out from the crowd, and improve your chances of landing a job.

    1. Work from anywhere

    Technology jobs â€“ especially within the emerging startup culture â€“ are well known for their flexibility and perks. Depending on the company, this could look like unlimited vacation time, telecommuting from another state or country, or work from home capabilities.Â 

    1. Flex hours

    Many programmers work flexible hours since all they need is a laptop and an internet connection. Companies usually have core hours where the team is required to log on for collaboration and meetings.Â 

    Tech companies that implement flex hours are less concerned with where you are, but rather that you get your work done. If you are a self-motivated high achiever who doesnâ€™t do well with micromanaging, you may love this perk.

    Since programmers work on computers most of the day, itâ€™s a great job to do via remote work. The benefit of technology is that companies can now hire teams globally. No longer are they hiring just local talent. Rather, they can hire the best of the best from anywhere in the world.

    1. Express your creativity

    Learning to code not only allows you to give machines instructions, but it also teaches you abstract thinking and problem-solving. In fact, problem-solving skills and creativity are key to becoming a successful computer programmer. Of course, youâ€™ll also need to know some coding languages to apply your knowledge.Â

    1. As Hunt and Gomez-Uribe remarked, the content recommendation feature is an incredibly powerful tool in retaining customers. Back in 2013, Netflix saw their recommendations driving over 75% of all content viewing, compared against consumer search21. As far as aligning corporate investment with the platform, Netflix in 2014 dedicated a team of 300 employees and spent $150M (around 3% of 2014 revenues) to improve their recommendation engine â€“ this dollar figure has likely continued to grow as the amount of content and subscribers has increased22.
    2. The newest investment that it seems Netflix is making to create a more customized and tailored platform experience is in connection with the artwork, or the thumbnails that subscribers see when browsing TV show and movie titles [6]. For example, there are nine different artworks for the Stranger Things show that users may see when browsing, depending on whether they have historically shown more interest in comedy, horror, or suspense in their viewing histories. However, this is in particular an area where Netflix should treat with caution, since there are downside risks of profiling and offending customers in a visually obvious way.
